Title: Re: HANAC versus Pistilli
Post by: bstewart on July 20, 2008, 02:08:29 PM
I know nothing about HANAC.  To my mind, housing is housing. As an outsider who didn't grow up here, the perennial Irish/German/Italian/Greek "you people take all the goodies" stuff just doesn't resonate.

I was raised Presbyterian, so I would rather that Scottish widows had preference.

As I understand it, the Sterns warehouse at 45th and Ditmars was considered for affordable senior housing. Then it was to be 20% senior housing and 80% condos, and on that understanding, the residential zoning was approved. The original developer died. Pistilli Group took on the property. They decided not to be bound by the deal that the former developer had made.

To jog my memory, I found this Queens Gazette article from Feb 2003 (http://www.qgazette.com/News/2003/0507/Front_page/001.html) and another from May 2003 (http://www.qgazette.com/News/2003/0507/Front_page/001.html)

(A bonus feature of the second article is a picture that some may want to use as a dartboard.)

This project may be different, in that there is actual money that will (presumably) go away if the purpose changes. But that public money could be a drop-in-the-bucket compared to the opportunity for condo development.

I don't like the size of the proposed building, and I hate to see the picturesque, if somewhat crumbling, old edifice go. But I've lived in the neighborhood for 28 years and I never set foot in that church. To be all indignant now, I'd feel a hypocrite.

Anyway, it will be fun to watch what trajectory this new project will take. (Fun in the sense of watching mischief that mostly involves other peoples' material interest.)
Title: Re: Pistilli Grand Manor Condominiums
Post by: Anthony11 on July 29, 2008, 01:39:26 PM
I've lived in the Astoria area my entire life and currently work in the real estate investment properties and construction.

Like many, I was excited about this project even before Pistilli was the owner and bought the rights to the building after the prior realtor died.  I kept a close eye on this property because it seemed like it would be a great investment, and possibly a place where my son or daughters could live in the future if I bought property there at the beginning.  That was 5 years ago and now that they're old enough to be on their own.

However, when I went on their "tours" and visited their open house, including additional visits by appointment, I can only say I was utterly disappointed.  The place had enormous potential, but the number of mistakes I found with the property was astounding and I've taken a pass on investing in the building.

For starters, the quality of the construction was poor.  It's to the point that they're just covering up mistakes instead of fixing them, including water damaged ceilings, eroding floors, wood laminate passed off as wood floors, numerous soft spots in the floors which will only lead to sagging floors, to broken window fixtures and springs that already need to be replaced before people even move in.  Paint was chipped in the model rooms, as well as damage to walls and fixtures before a person has even moved in.

The layouts of the units are terrible.  One thing they teach designers and architects immediately is not to waste space.  The majority of the units have terribly wasted space including semi walk-in closets that aren't true walk in closets, long corridors to bathrooms, obstructed angles to bathrooms, uneven ceiling levels preventing anyone from hanging light fixtures or ceiling fans, on top of odd corners and nooks that can only fit decorations or small furnishings.  The space of the units is large enough that these spaces could have been utilized more efficiently.

The appliances are regular day bargain basement items you find at Home Depot.  When building a multiple dwelling building, the ideal is to save money on appliances by getting them in bulk.  Having accounts with Home Depot, Lowe's and other retailers allows you the ability to get quality materials for cheaper prices.  Considering Pistilli needed 200 appliances minimum, he could have even gotten great contractor deals directly from manufacturers (instead of third party retailers like Home Depot).  But Pistilli took the cheap route and installed all low end products.  Every stove, dishwasher, toilet, sink, bath tub, shower head, refrigeration unit and microwave he installed can be found at Home Depot, and marketed towards the middle income class families (I checked this on my own).  The "stainless steel" products are faux stainless steel... a great seller's tool that people will not notice on first walkthroughs.  The product is a metallic tape, permanently sealed to a plastic fridge to give the appeal of stainless steel.  It doesn't scrape or tear like normal tape, but will wear and tear over the years.  It's an extraordinarily cheaper solution to stainless steel than actually getting stainless steal products.  To add value to your condo, these products should be replaced immediately, which will cost you upfront money.

My final concern is the price.  Unfortunately, there is no true competitor in his market.  Pistilli Grand Manor does not have a single condo competitor within a 10 block radius, and the closest 3 markets are Garden Bay Condos, Barclay Gardens and Shore Towers Condos... each offering completely different amenities and values for buyers.  His pricing of ~$1 PSF is slightly pricey, but again, there is no true competitor to challenge his price.  The average asking price of $400K for $500 PSF is also relatively high compared to 3 aforementioned condos.  The only difference is the GB, BG & ST have more to offer than just a 200 unit building with a garage (where you still rent a space).  ST offers views of Manhattan, tennis courts, balconies and other high end amenities.  GB & BG offer homestyle ownership of a condo, with outdoor patios, grassy backyards and a limited number of neighbors, thus their pricing plateau is $150K lower on average, offering a much more cost efficient alternative.

I strongly believe this property could have been worth this asking price of $500 PSF, had the conditions been right.  The appliances, the construction, the layouts and amenities should have been top notch to ask for $500 PSF, but they fell below average expectations and underwhelmed at best.  Though his prices are negotiable, it seems the money he is willing to lose on payment for the unit, will have to be reinvested by the buyer back into the property to make it enjoyable.  Thus, purchasers will be saving on the signing price, but paying for personal renovations and upgrades to make the space their own, and make the unit more profitable in maintenance costs in the future for Pistilli.

As a realtor, an investor, a prospective buyer and a father, I would strongly recommend anyone interested in this property to do their research into alternative purchases.  The money you spend buying a unit here might be better spent at another condo like Garden Bay or Barclay Gardens.  Or, you can always wait for Pistilli's next project, which will be built diagonally across from his current building since he bought the retail space that has Astoria Bakery, the cleaners and brick oven pizza restaurant.  When their leases expire, he will raze that space to build another condo unit.  The last lease belongs to Astoria Bakery which will expire in 2009.

Title: Re: Pistilli Grand Manor Condominiums
Post by: Gleason on November 13, 2008, 09:26:44 AM
You are right. Take a look at factory loft conversions in Brooklyn or even the Bronx. Excellent work. What happend to Eagle Electric, L I Savings Bank on 30th Ave, and the Steinway Piano are embarrassment that are an exercise in bad taste.

You questions are easy to answer and all but impossible to solve unless things change.

You have a small clique that runs Astoria and have been doing so for a very long period of time. They know each other and have no real desire (or incentive for that matter) to open up their little clubhouse. Years ago when the rest of the city was burning this made some sense, but now the city has moved forward and this little group has lot touch with progress. To ensure a quiet public, any avenue for discussion or information is blocked. Newspapers, community board, officials, and what passes for civics.

Good luck in even trying to get a serious discussion.

As the attitude (even on this board) demonstrates, the first reaction is to deny there is a problem, and the second (when their face is rubbed in it) is to snarl that you should move as others (more desperate and not as discriminating perhaps?) would be happy to fill your shoes. Check out the 'human feces thread' as a stellar example of public discourse in this community.

So you have the small time small town local talent (with no taste or sophistication) throwing up cheaply built tenements and ready to milk as much as they can as quickly as they can. As someone wrote on Queens Crap, they have written off the community and are ripping out the pipes.
 
Architects on the community board are involved in building in the community, everyone has a fratboy approach to an empty lot - "lets see how much we can make." Many people making choices on  our future don't even live here. The largest contributor to politician's campaigns are developers. Your tax money is used to subsidize them, not provide services to your family. Remember that when your taxes take a big jump next year.

When that stucco starts to fall off, fades, and gets dirty in about 20 years these developers will either be dead or in Florida.  :x

The west of Queens is targeted for a massive jump in population and - with no discussion of infrastructure to support it - a massive decline in quality of life. Thoughout the city, with a smirk, its called the 'Wild West.' And Community Board One is famed as the belly of the beast. Go to another community board meeting and the difference is glaring.

Go down to LIC or Dutch Kills. Look at communities hoodwinked and betrayed, or if that failed, simply ignored.

That is our future.  :cry:

Title: Re: Pistilli Riverview East Apartments
Post by: NYCMacUser on November 15, 2008, 08:07:06 AM
Stachybotrys is not as toxic as it's reputation. There are many other types of mold that are much more dangerous and insidious. If it were I, I would not rely on a home testing kit. I would call in a professional to do a full house inspection. They should take air samples and swab samples from every area of the place. I understand that there are some infrared cameras that can even detect mold that has not yet discolored enough to be visible. Before any attempts to remove and/or clean the mold you should know the type of mold you are dealing with, how sever the growth is, it's source, and then the proper process to treat, prevent and permanently remove the mold. If you own this apartment, this is an investment in your future.

Title: Re: Pistilli Riverview East Apartments
Post by: k4sting on December 05, 2008, 12:20:24 PM
FYI for the people who have posted issues with water and mold issues
this can be a health problem and very expensive to resolve properly...
(the information below is from a general web search)
Toxic mold, which can develop when an organic substance comes in contact with water
and can spread to many surfaces throughout a home, is a problem in buildings across
New York City.
Any indoor mold, including species that are not considered toxic, can, in sufficient
quantities, have adverse effects on susceptible populations, such as children, the elderly,
and asthmatics. Exposure to sufficient quantities of any kind of indoor mold is likely to
aggravate asthma conditions and provoke other severe allergic reactions. An additional
long-term effect of mold exposure is that it can increase a childs chances of becoming
asthmatic; even fetal exposure can increase the risk of developing asthma.
Mold destroys the surface it grows on by digesting the organic material. It can rot wood,
drywall, and other construction materials, eventually causing structural damage.
Roof leaks, faulty plumbing, flooding, and high levels of humidity can all
contribute to destructive indoor mold growth.
How do I get rid of mold?
It is impossible to get rid of all mold and mold spores indoors; some mold spores will be found floating through the air and in house dust.  The mold spores will not grow if moisture is not present.  Indoor mold growth can and should be prevented or controlled by controlling moisture indoors.  If there is mold growth in your home, you must clean up the mold and fix the water problem.  If you clean up the mold, but don't fix the water problem, then, most likely, the mold problem will come back.

Title: Re: Pistilli Riverview East Apartments
Post by: johnny4evah! on December 17, 2008, 01:06:53 PM
Aside from obvious health problems brought on by mold, water damage can lead to serious structural problems if it's chronic. If it's an older building (like most of the homes surrounding the Pistilli place with wood beams) water damage can lead to termite infestation-a pretty commom problem here in Astoria. If the exterior of the building is covered in that man-made stucco stuff mold will set in and grow if there is a leak. I think the Eagle building-er, I mean Pistilli building- is covered in EIF. That synthetic stucco stuff isn't all that it's cracked up to be. It's been associated with moisture problems. If the leaks are interior in origin, then you have a whole different can of worms!

http://www.almosthome.com/eifsFaq.htm

(I'm not a contractor, but I wouldn't use this stuff on my home.)

Hope the above info helps! Not trying to scare anyone, but alittle knowledge can be a terrible thing!

Title: Re: Pistilli Riverview East Apartments
Post by: NYCMacUser on December 26, 2008, 10:08:53 AM
Although co-ops and condominiums are both considered "common interest developments" a co-op building is owned by a cooperative housing corporation, while in a condominium, each unit owner owns their individual apartment. Co-op owners do not own their units but they own a share in the cooperative corporation, and that co-op share gives them sole right to their living space.

Title: Re: Pistilli Riverview East question
Post by: Sweeper on January 23, 2009, 08:42:58 AM
Magnetic sheets are great in hiding the symptom, but they are not a cure. It is not uncommon for cold air to come through the vent, but it is always wrong. The purpose of any "vent" is to remove air from the space. I would definitely talk to the super, but do some research first. It can be very difficult to fix especially when a project has already been completed.

Title: Re: Pistilli Grand Manor Condominiums
Post by: slappy76 on March 03, 2009, 02:04:29 PM
Well.. I'm officially an Astorian. Having lived in Kew Garden Hills practically all my life this is a nice change of scenery. Unfortunately my fiance insisted on this PGM complex. She just can't tolerate roaches.. so older buildings are a no-no. Well I wish I read a little more online before committing to this 1 year rental. Aside from the totally craptacular no-frills appliances. The warping Pergo-laminate flooring. Here's some things that aren't mentioned:

1) There's no cooking gas at ALL. Having spoken with someone that has lived here since last summer, that hasn't changed for 7 months. This adds $$$ to my bottom line when I have to spend extra money on take out. Buy new temporary electric appliances (crock pot, convection ovens, etc). Adds to my electric bill.

2) Right now as of this writing there is no water. They turned it off without any notice this morning. No time to bottle or store water in a pot.

3) The doorman is only there for 1 shift. Which is not a big deal but... (see next gripe)

4) There are no security cameras to speak of for such a huge place. It's not a dangerous neighborhood but anything to deter riff-raffs would be nice.

5) It's kind of eerie living in a building with 180 units and having only 10-20 apts filled. Nice if you like to go streaking down the halls in the middle of the night.

6) Good luck if you live in one of the apartments in the back of the building. You'll have to walk from the front of the building to take the elevator in order to walk all the way to back. Worse yet.. if you pay for their parking lot.. you'll have to walk from the parking lot (back) to the front and all the way back again. Good luck with those bags of groceries.

7) Pistilli, in their infinite wisdom, installed a high gloss marble floor at the top of the steps extending from the glass foyer. So during this last snow storm (before the superintendent puts out the salt or mats) I almost break my neck. That is a lawsuit just waiting to happen. Remember as condo owner that's on your head.

I'm sure I'll have more complaints as the weeks turn into months..

-Slappy

Title: Re: Pistilli Grand Manor-Astoria Queens

I used to live in a Pistilli rental building with a huge bed bug infestation problem.  They crawl through the walls from neighboring apartments, and invade the whole building.  When I found out we had them, I called the management office and raised all kinds of hell.  It took me actually quoting the law for them to send over an exterminator 3 times to fully extinguish them all.  They dealt with the problem but it took some pushing.  The management had us go to all the apartments to see if we could find out the full extent of the problem, and it turned out that a bunch of people had them, and were not saying or doing anything about it.  These things were biting their children, and they just let the problem persist.  We ended up getting the whole building exterminated numerous times, but in the midst of all that, my lease was up, and I took the nightmare I was living in, as a sign from up high, to get the hell out.  I will never ever live in another Pistilli building.   That problem was just the last straw.  He has a bad reputation as a slumlord and many realtors won't even work with the guy.

I know of all the things I've said and read, the clear thing would be to forget about this unit but I think if it's renovated, there could be potential because of the location and the good size. I've looked at those apartments...and there were a couple of issues I had with them:

- Windows have no screens and they are too large - need custom made shades & screens (more $$$).

- The range hood above the stove is blank inside (there's no fan motor)...it's only there for decoration.

- The laminated flooring they used scratches easily.

- And even though heat is included in the maint. you need electricity to run the fan motor and spread the heat and a/c throughout your apartment. Your electric bill is going to be high.

-The gym is too far into the lower level - it seems like a dungeon down there.

But the worst part was the bed bugs.  I have called so many times to speak to the property manager, but I keep being sent to a voice mail box   that is full. and can  not accept any additional calls.   I have sent e-mails but I get no respond.  Finally I made believe I was looking to rent an apartment,  and they call me right away.  so many apartment became available because tenant were constantly moving out.   the problem with BED BUGS IS SERIOUS  AND PISTILLI'S  NEGLIGENCE  MAKES IT  WORST.   I had to battle with them to get out of there.  Never again will I fall into their misleading advertisement. I HAD heard bad things about the Pistilli Owners, but I thought people deserve a second chance and thinking they made a new development, they would be more caring and responsible owners, I was wrong.   I don't need a  faulty  MAKE BELIEVE luxury building . I need a solid  responsible and reputable owner. OR MANAGING COMPANY.   So think about it . do your own research.

As i have said before, pretty much everywhere i have lived the management has been poor to terrible. I have yet to come across a landlord or super who is on top of things. Mind you i'm making middle class wages here, so obviously the more money you make the better the living. However with middle class wages you get what you can get in the NYC area. Any who i've had issue with various things in the apt at the Pistilli building but all in all its not that bad (as of yet) and aside from the rent cost. I've been here for a little over 6 months and haven't minded dealing with the Pistilli ppl-the good so far is outweighing the bad by a good amount.

Side Note
-Not related to Astoria or the Pistilli building, has anyone seeked out apts in long island, near the long island mall.

Title: Pistilli Riverview East - Monsoon Season
Post by: suigenerous1 on May 04, 2010, 10:29:58 AM
After several failed attemps over two years Pistilli has failed to to fix the flooding issues in this building. Several residents in the building have filed complaints with HPD (Housing Preservation and Development) and are seeking legal advice on filing a suit in civil court.

Go to the youtube to view videos of a handful of apartments that were flooded.
http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LU-z7bM0adA&feature=related (http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LU-z7bM0adA&feature=related)

I have been served with eviction papers, been to court, granted and Order to Show Cause (OSC) which stops the eviction process, and given a court date of 7/16/2010 to argue the case in front of a judge. This is in addition to the existing court date I have on 7/21/2010 which is a follow-up to the court proceedings from 6/14/2010.
It would be great if residents in the building would join me in going through the court process. I understand why they are reluctant to do so. This has been a miserable process and because the apartments are not rent stabilized, the tenants here make too much money to qualify for legal assistance and therefore must pay out of pocket for legal representation. I have been representing myself which makes the process even more frustrating because I often learn a better or quicker way I could have filed or done things- after the fact. Live and learn. I'm sure learning a lot!

Title: Re: Daily News is Looking to Interview Pistilli Tenants
Post by: Bexlyspeed on July 23, 2010, 08:56:41 AM
I live in the building across the street from Astoria Park. My Girlfriend owns the Apartment and is probably one of the frist people to live in the building. we have had some minor problems with leaks but i have to say everything was repaired in a timely manner. not to say i have not heard the horror stories about massive leaks and whatnot, i know them to be true and i am not really clear on why our luck has been so good.
I find that the maintenance staff has always taken care of us and i think they are good guys that do a pretty good job around the building. Especially now with the pool open and all the trash that gets dumped around the perimeter of the building. its never there for long although it is a bit messier on the backside of the building.
now building management is a different story. i believe we are on our second building manager since the site has opened. the first guy was totally useless, i dont even remember his name. now its run by Pitsilli's son and nephew (both named michael) and i think we deal mostly with the nephew. he doesnt seem to care about anything and he takes his sweet time responding to your calls. so now we just go straight to the supervisor of the maintenance crew, his name is Robert and he is top class. always returns calls promptly and when he tells you a time that somebody will be there they are there. i guess i'm just trying to say that not everyone in the building is bad and i hope that if this daily news thing brings about any changes that its to pitstillui and building management and not to the hard working maintenance crew.
Title: Re: Daily News is Looking to Interview Pistilli Tenants
Post by: krocker on July 23, 2010, 04:31:14 PM
I also live in Riverview East and feel like only bad things are ever said about this building, which is a shame and a bit misleading, IMO.  I think the complaints of a smattering of people in a large building, while definitely justified, are being blown out of proportion. 

I fully admit that I am no fan of the Pistilli management style either (ie - slow response time to complaints, wanting to do things on the cheap whenever possible).  But I have to say that I have been, on the whole, very happy with my apartment which is large and very nice and has not had the problems mentioned by other tenants.  I've also been quite happy with Robert the super, happy with the other building staff who work very hard and long hours, and happy with our neighbors.

I've been biting my tongue on this for a while, because it's clearly not popular to defend any Pistilli property, but I think it's only fair that an alternate point of view is heard.

On the other hand Belkis the office manager is very hard to get in touch with and I do agree with you that if you place a call for her, you will never get a call back or you will be pushed to one of her many office assistants. I live in a Pistilli owned building and here is how I get things fixed:
Call every single day (gradually increasing to twice and three times a day) until the person you need to talk to is not "out for lunch", "not in today", "hold on, oh he/she's in a meeting".  It takes at least a week and is infuriating, but it works.  I also find that quoting housing code works somewhat quicker if you happen to have an issue of that level (like having the right to live in a vermin-free environment).

Properties include, Pistilli Grand Manor, The Astral and other properties that are owned and managed by Pistilli Realty Group and/or subsidiary firms.


Requirements

  • You must be a current resident of a Pistilli property.
  • You must be able to write and express your opinion without using foul or inappropriate language.
  • You will report relevant & important information related to the building which you are representing.
  • You agree to publish all appropriate comments* including those that represent dissenting opinions.
  • You will respond to all comments in a professional and fair manner.

Do You Know Where Your Security Deposit Is?

Title: Re: All discussion concerning Pistilli Riverview East, Grand Manor, and other properties
Post by: Hanahlly on August 02, 2010, 01:45:04 PM
It's important to know if your security deposit is in Pistilli's bank for many reasons. The bank, First Central Savings Bank, was recently fined $100,000 by the FDIC and ordered to pay restitution to account holders affected by the bank's failure to disclose an "interest-floor" on applicable accounts. First Central is on multiple industry lists of "troubled" banks and the March, 25, 2010 rating and review by The Street, gives First Central Savings Bank a Safety Rating of E, Very Weak Financial Strength.

    The E rating means that, in our opinion, this institution currently demonstrates what we consider to be significant weaknesses and has also failed some of the basic test we use to identify fiscal stability. Therefore, even in a favorable economic environment, it is our opinion that depositors or creditors could incur significant risks.

For more information, you can read the blog post http://thetruthaboutpistillirivervieweast.wordpress.com/2010/08/02/is-your-security-deposit-in-pistillis-bank/ or click on the individual information sources listed below.


Sources:
FDIC Order: http://docs.google.com/viewer?a=v&q=cache:7-BeAbFHywIJ:www.fdic.gov/bank/individual/enforcement/2010-02-29.pdf+first+central+savings+bank+fdic&hl=en&gl=us&pid=bl&srcid=ADGEESiV143msTcKMe6uhrcG9p6B14wqWVxtXe8yxQww0PTX5_0vhIa2bjl22eo6YrrhbEET1q-iNcHwGGC2rY9PLg3xgXDbV36nYV8x1UtbW_QDsSBrahsHBtXl5uycj4OvVOAViYlu&sig=AHIEtbSs1wP_Yq2QVPRkEhKx2KxKPwO1XA
The Street Rating: http://docs.google.com/viewer?a=v&q=cache:Qz0CXD4j8MkJ:www.thestreet.com/tsc/ratings/pdfdata/WEBRATS/B/FREECSU_0F1E0E41-6F80-4C3E-B36A-4E50391B2130.PDF+first+central+savings+bank+glen+cove&hl=en&gl=us&pid=bl&srcid=ADGEESgfDnMiI1eJZvvpDADRB0XUUh_g92aTc0QG4kXBxmqOO0V8XkwNCwGqi8XaaJxLxyKiTqZHk3tp4NB_hLY_p9OSpDJCw-Wmum__eEyerL59u3APq9xFQeKGiRmJK0IJ5J3lOMif&sig=AHIEtbQS3IOYGdsB2_mOfACh9-i8ZUk4Vg
